id=\"user-content-update-channels\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThere are currently three release channels for binaries: \u003ccode\u003estable\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003enightly\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003emaster\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003estable\u003c/code\u003e is the default channel, and many of its changes have been tested by users of the \u003ccode\u003enightly\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003emaster\u003c/code\u003e channels.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003enightly\u003c/code\u003e channel has releases scheduled to build every day around midnight UTC, for a snapshot of the project's new patches and changes. This is the \u003cstrong\u003erecommended channel for regular users\u003c/strong\u003e of yt-dlp. The \u003ccode\u003enightly\u003c/code\u003e releases are available from \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/yt-dlp/yt-dlp-nightly-builds/releases\"\u003eyt-dlp/yt-dlp-nightly-builds\u003c/a\u003e or as development releases of the \u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp\u003c/code\u003e PyPI package (which can be installed with pip's \u003ccode\u003e--pre\u003c/code\u003e flag).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003emaster\u003c/code\u003e channel features releases that are built after each push to the master branch, and these will have the very latest fixes and additions, but may also be more prone to regressions. They are available from \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/yt-dlp/yt-dlp-master-builds/releases\"\u003eyt-dlp/yt-dlp-master-builds\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWhen using \u003ccode\u003e--update\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003e-U\u003c/code\u003e, a release binary will only update to its current channel.\n\u003ccode\u003e--update-to CHANNEL\u003c/code\u003e can be used to switch to a different channel when a newer version is available. \u003ccode\u003e--update-to [CHANNEL@]TAG\u003c/code\u003e can also be used to upgrade or downgrade to specific tags from a channel.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou may also use \u003ccode\u003e--update-to \u0026lt;repository\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003e\u0026lt;owner\u0026gt;/\u0026lt;repository\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e) to update to a channel on a completely different repository. Be careful with what repository you are updating to though, there is no verification done for binaries from different repositories.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eExample usage:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp --update-to master\u003c/code\u003e switch to the \u003ccode\u003emaster\u003c/code\u003e channel and update to its latest release\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp --update-to stable@2023.07.06\u003c/code\u003e upgrade/downgrade to release to \u003ccode\u003estable\u003c/code\u003e channel tag \u003ccode\u003e2023.07.06\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp --update-to 2023.10.07\u003c/code\u003e upgrade/downgrade to tag \u003ccode\u003e2023.10.07\u003c/code\u003e if it exists on the current channel\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp --update-to example/yt-dlp@2023.09.24\u003c/code\u003e upgrade/downgrade to the release from the \u003ccode\u003eexample/yt-dlp\u003c/code\u003e repository, tag \u003ccode\u003e2023.09.24\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp and \u003ccode\u003epyinstaller\u003c/code\u003e (plus any of yt-dlp's \u003ca href=\"#dependencies\"\u003eoptional dependencies\u003c/a\u003e if needed). The executable will be built for the same CPU architecture as the Python used.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou can run the following commands:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"python devscripts/install_deps.py --include-extra pyinstaller\npython devscripts/make_lazy_extractors.py\npython -m bundle.pyinstaller\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epython devscripts/install_deps.py --include-extra pyinstaller\npython devscripts/make_lazy_extractors.py\npython -m bundle.pyinstaller\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOn some systems, you may need to use \u003ccode\u003epy\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003epython3\u003c/code\u003e instead of \u003ccode\u003epython\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003epython -m bundle.pyinstaller\u003c/code\u003e accepts any arguments that can be passed to \u003ccode\u003epyinstaller\u003c/code\u003e, such as \u003ccode\u003e--onefile/-F\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e--onedir/-D\u003c/code\u003e, which is further \u003ca href=\"https://pyinstaller.org/en/stable/usage.html#what-to-generate\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003edocumented here\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote\u003c/strong\u003e: Pyinstaller versions below 4.4 \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/pyinstaller/pyinstaller#requirements-and-tested-platforms\"\u003edo not support\u003c/a\u003e Python installed from the Windows store without using a virtual environment.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eImportant\u003c/strong\u003e: Running \u003ccode\u003epyinstaller\u003c/code\u003e directly \u003cstrong\u003einstead of\u003c/strong\u003e using \u003ccode\u003epython -m bundle.pyinstaller\u003c/code\u003e is \u003cstrong\u003enot\u003c/strong\u003e officially supported. This may or may not work correctly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003ePlatform-independent Binary (UNIX)\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-platform-independent-binary-unix\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Platform-independent Binary (UNIX)\" href=\"#platform-independent-binary-unix\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou will need the build tools \u003ccode\u003epython\u003c/code\u003e (3.10+), \u003ccode\u003ezip\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003emake\u003c/code\u003e (GNU), \u003ccode\u003epandoc\u003c/code\u003e* and \u003ccode\u003epytest\u003c/code\u003e*.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAfter installing these, simply run \u003ccode\u003emake\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou can also run \u003ccode\u003emake yt-dlp\u003c/code\u003e instead to compile only the binary without updating any of the additional files. class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"-h, --help                      Print this help text and exit\n--version                       Print program version and exit\n-U, --update                    Update this program to the latest version\n--no-update                     Do not check for updates (default)\n--update-to [CHANNEL]@[TAG]     Upgrade/downgrade to a specific version.\n                                CHANNEL can be a repository as well. CHANNEL\n                                and TAG default to \u0026quot;stable\u0026quot; and \u0026quot;latest\u0026quot;\n                                respectively if omitted; See \u0026quot;UPDATE\u0026quot; for\n                                details. Supported channels: stable,\n                                nightly, master\n-i, --ignore-errors             Ignore download and postprocessing errors.\n                                The download will be considered successful\n                                even if the postprocessing fails\n--no-abort-on-error             Continue with next video on download errors;\n                                e.g. to skip unavailable videos in a\n                                playlist (default)\n--abort-on-error                Abort downloading of further videos if an\n                                error occurs (Alias: --no-ignore-errors)\n--list-extractors               List all supported extractors and exit\n--extractor-descriptions        Output descriptions of all supported\n                                extractors and exit\n--use-extractors NAMES          Extractor names to use separated by commas.\n                                You can also use regexes, \u0026quot;all\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;default\u0026quot;\n                                and \u0026quot;end\u0026quot; (end URL matching); e.g. --ies\n                                \u0026quot;holodex.*,end,youtube\u0026quot;. Prefix the name\n                                with a \u0026quot;-\u0026quot; to exclude it, e.g. --ies\n                                default,-generic. Use --list-extractors for\n                                a list of extractor names. (Alias: --ies)\n--default-search PREFIX         Use this prefix for unqualified URLs. E.g.\n                                \u0026quot;gvsearch2:python\u0026quot; downloads two videos from\n                                google videos for the search term \u0026quot;python\u0026quot;.\n                                Use the value \u0026quot;auto\u0026quot; to let yt-dlp guess\n                                (\u0026quot;auto_warning\u0026quot; to emit a warning when\n                                guessing). \u0026quot;error\u0026quot; just throws an error. The\n                                default value \u0026quot;fixup_error\u0026quot; repairs broken\n                                URLs, but emits an error if this is not\n                                possible instead of searching\n--ignore-config                 Don't load any more configuration files\n                                except those given to --config-locations.\n                                For backward compatibility, if this option\n                                is found inside the system configuration\n                                file, the user configuration is not loaded.\n                                (Alias: --no-config)\n--no-config-locations           Do not load any custom configuration files\n                                (default). When given inside a configuration\n                                file, ignore all previous --config-locations\n                                defined in the current file\n--config-locations PATH         Location of the main configuration file;\n                                either the path to the config or its\n                                containing directory (\u0026quot;-\u0026quot; for stdin). Can be\n                                used multiple times and inside other\n                                configuration files\n--plugin-dirs DIR               Path to an additional directory to search\n                                for plugins. This option can be used\n                                multiple times to add multiple directories.\n                                Use \u0026quot;default\u0026quot; to search the default plugin\n                                directories (default)\n--no-plugin-dirs                Clear plugin directories to search,\n                                including defaults and those provided by\n                                previous --plugin-dirs\n--js-runtimes RUNTIME[:PATH]    Additional JavaScript runtime to enable,\n                                with an optional location for the runtime\n                                (either the path to the binary or its\n                                containing directory). This option can be\n                                used multiple times to enable multiple\n                                runtimes. Supported runtimes are (in order\n                                of priority, from highest to lowest): deno,\n                                node, quickjs, bun. Only \u0026quot;deno\u0026quot; is enabled\n                                by default. The highest priority runtime\n                                that is both enabled and available will be\n                                used. In order to use a lower priority\n                                runtime when \u0026quot;deno\u0026quot; is available, --no-js-\n                                runtimes needs to be passed before enabling\n                                other runtimes\n--no-js-runtimes                Clear JavaScript runtimes to enable,\n                                including defaults and those provided by\n                                previous --js-runtimes\n--remote-components COMPONENT   Remote components to allow yt-dlp to fetch\n                                when required. This option is currently not\n                                needed if you are using an official\n                                executable or have the requisite version of\n                                the yt-dlp-ejs package installed. You can\n                                use this option multiple times to allow\n                                multiple components. Supported values:\n                                ejs:npm (external JavaScript components from\n                                npm), ejs:github (external JavaScript\n                                components from yt-dlp-ejs GitHub). By\n                                default, no remote components are allowed\n--no-remote-components          Disallow fetching of all remote components,\n                                including any previously allowed by\n                                --remote-components or defaults.\n--flat-playlist                 Do not extract a playlist's URL result\n                                entries; some entry metadata may be missing\n                                and downloading may be bypassed\n--no-flat-playlist              Fully extract the videos of a playlist\n                                (default)\n--live-from-start               Download livestreams from the start.\n                                Currently experimental and only supported\n                                for YouTube and Twitch\n--no-live-from-start            Download livestreams from the current time\n                                (default)\n--wait-for-video MIN[-MAX]      Wait for scheduled streams to become\n                                available. Pass the minimum number of\n                                seconds (or range) to wait between retries\n--no-wait-for-video             Do not wait for scheduled streams (default)\n--mark-watched                  Mark videos watched (even with --simulate)\n--no-mark-watched               Do not mark videos watched (default)\n--color [STREAM:]POLICY         Whether to emit color codes in output,\n                                optionally prefixed by the STREAM (stdout or\n                                stderr) to apply the setting to. Can be one\n                                of \u0026quot;always\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;auto\u0026quot; (default), \u0026quot;never\u0026quot;, or\n                                \u0026quot;no_color\u0026quot; (use non color terminal\n                                sequences). Use \u0026quot;auto-tty\u0026quot; or \u0026quot;no_color-tty\u0026quot;\n                                to decide based on terminal support only.\n                                Can be used multiple times\n--compat-options OPTS           Options that can help keep compatibility\n                                with youtube-dl or youtube-dlc\n                                configurations by reverting some of the\n                                changes made in yt-dlp. See \u0026quot;Differences in\n                                default behavior\u0026quot; for details\n--alias ALIASES OPTIONS         Create aliases for an option string. Unless\n                                an alias starts with a dash \u0026quot;-\u0026quot;, it is\n                                prefixed with \u0026quot;--\u0026quot;. Arguments are parsed\n                                according to the Python string formatting\n                                mini-language. E.g. --alias get-audio,-X \u0026quot;-S\n                                aext:{0},abr -x --audio-format {0}\u0026quot; creates\n                                options \u0026quot;--get-audio\u0026quot; and \u0026quot;-X\u0026quot; that takes an\n                                argument (ARG0) and expands to \u0026quot;-S\n                                aext:ARG0,abr -x --audio-format ARG0\u0026quot;. All\n                                defined aliases are listed in the --help\n                                output. Alias options can trigger more\n                                aliases; so be careful to avoid defining\n                                recursive options. As a safety measure, each\n                                alias may be triggered a maximum of 100\n                                times. This option can be used multiple times\n-t, --preset-alias PRESET       Applies a predefined set of options. e.g.\n                                --preset-alias mp3. The following presets\n                                are available: mp3, aac, mp4, mkv, sleep.\n                                See the \u0026quot;Preset Aliases\u0026quot; section at the end\n                                for more info. E.g.\n                                \"gvsearch2:python\" downloads two videos from\n                                google videos for the search term \"python\".\n                                Use the value \"auto\" to let yt-dlp guess\n                                (\"auto_warning\" to emit a warning when\n                                guessing). \"error\" just throws an error. When given inside a configuration\n                                file, ignore all previous --config-locations\n                                defined in the current file\n--config-locations PATH         Location of the main configuration file;\n                                either the path to the config or its\n                                containing directory (\"-\" for stdin). Can be\n                                used multiple times and inside other\n                                configuration files\n--plugin-dirs DIR               Path to an additional directory to search\n                                for plugins. Only \"deno\" is enabled\n                                by default. The highest priority runtime\n                                that is both enabled and available will be\n                                used. This option is currently not\n                                needed if you are using an official\n                                executable or have the requisite version of\n                                the yt-dlp-ejs package installed. Arguments are parsed\n                                according to the Python string formatting\n                                mini-language. E.g. --alias get-audio,-X \"-S\n                                aext:{0},abr -x --audio-format {0}\" creates\n                                options \"--get-audio\" and \"-X\" that takes an\n                                argument (ARG0) and expands to \"-S\n                                aext:ARG0,abr -x --audio-format ARG0\". You can also simply\n                                specify a field to match if the field is\n                                present, use \u0026quot;!field\u0026quot; to check if the field\n                                is not present, and \u0026quot;\u0026amp;\u0026quot; to check multiple\n                                conditions. If used multiple times,\n                                the filter matches if at least one of the\n                                conditions is met. Number of times to retry on file access\n                                error (default is 3), or \u0026quot;infinite\u0026quot;\n--fragment-retries RETRIES      Number of retries for a fragment (default is\n                                10), or \u0026quot;infinite\u0026quot; (DASH, hlsnative and ISM)\n--retry-sleep [TYPE:]EXPR       Time to sleep between retries in seconds\n                                (optionally) prefixed by the type of retry\n                                (http (default), fragment, file_access,\n                                extractor) to apply the sleep to. EXPR can\n                                be a number, linear=START[:END[:STEP=1]] or\n                                exp=START[:END[:BASE=2]]. This option can be\n                                used multiple times to set the sleep for the\n                                different retry types, e.g. --retry-sleep\n                                linear=1::2 --retry-sleep fragment:exp=1:20\n--skip-unavailable-fragments    Skip unavailable fragments for DASH,\n                                hlsnative and ISM downloads (default)\n                                (Alias: --no-abort-on-unavailable-fragments)\n--abort-on-unavailable-fragments\n                                Abort download if a fragment is unavailable\n                                (Alias: --no-skip-unavailable-fragments)\n--keep-fragments                Keep downloaded fragments on disk after\n                                downloading is finished\n--no-keep-fragments             Delete downloaded fragments after\n                                downloading is finished (default)\n--buffer-size SIZE              Size of download buffer, e.g. 1024 or 16K\n                                (default is 1024)\n--resize-buffer                 The buffer size is automatically resized\n                                from an initial value of --buffer-size\n                                (default)\n--no-resize-buffer              Do not automatically adjust the buffer size\n--http-chunk-size SIZE          Size of a chunk for chunk-based HTTP\n                                downloading, e.g. 10485760 or 10M (default\n                                is disabled). May be useful for bypassing\n                                bandwidth throttling imposed by a webserver\n                                (experimental)\n--playlist-random               Download playlist videos in random order\n--lazy-playlist                 Process entries in the playlist as they are\n                                received. This disables n_entries,\n                                --playlist-random and --playlist-reverse\n--no-lazy-playlist              Process videos in the playlist only after\n                                the entire playlist is parsed (default)\n--hls-use-mpegts                Use the mpegts container for HLS videos;\n                                allowing some players to play the video\n                                while downloading, and reducing the chance\n                                of file corruption if download is\n                                interrupted. This is enabled by default for\n                                live streams\n--no-hls-use-mpegts             Do not use the mpegts container for HLS\n                                videos. This is default when not downloading\n                                live streams\n--download-sections REGEX       Download only chapters that match the\n                                regular expression. A \u0026quot;*\u0026quot; prefix denotes\n                                time-range instead of chapter. Negative\n                                timestamps are calculated from the end.\n                                \u0026quot;*from-url\u0026quot; can be used to download between\n                                the \u0026quot;start_time\u0026quot; and \u0026quot;end_time\u0026quot; extracted\n                                from the URL. Needs ffmpeg. This option can\n                                be used multiple times to download multiple\n                                sections, e.g. --download-sections\n                                \u0026quot;*10:15-inf\u0026quot; --download-sections \u0026quot;intro\u0026quot;\n--downloader [PROTO:]NAME       Name or path of the external downloader to\n                                use (optionally) prefixed by the protocols\n                                (http, ftp, m3u8, dash, rstp, rtmp, mms) to\n                                use it for. Currently supports native,\n                                aria2c, axel, curl, ffmpeg, httpie, wget.\n                                You can use this option multiple times to\n                                set different downloaders for different\n                                protocols. E.g. --downloader aria2c\n                                --downloader \u0026quot;dash,m3u8:native\u0026quot; will use\n                                aria2c for http/ftp downloads, and the\n                                native downloader for dash/m3u8 downloads\n                                (Alias: --external-downloader)\n--downloader-args NAME:ARGS     Give these arguments to the external\n                                downloader. Specify the downloader name and\n                                the arguments separated by a colon \u0026quot;:\u0026quot;. For\n                                ffmpeg, arguments can be passed to different\n                                positions using the same syntax as\n                                --postprocessor-args. You can use this\n                                option multiple times to give different\n                                arguments to different downloaders (Alias:\n                                --external-downloader-args)\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e-N, --concurrent-fragments N    Number of fragments of a dash/hlsnative\n                                video that should be downloaded concurrently\n                                (default is 1)\n-r, --limit-rate RATE           Maximum download rate in bytes per second,\n                                e.g. 50K or 4.2M\n--throttled-rate RATE           Minimum download rate in bytes per second\n                                below which throttling is assumed and the\n                                video data is re-extracted, e.g. 100K\n-R, --retries RETRIES           Number of retries (default is 10), or\n                                \"infinite\"\n--file-access-retries RETRIES   Number of times to retry on file access\n                                error (default is 3), or \"infinite\"\n--fragment-retries RETRIES      Number of retries for a fragment (default is\n                                10), or \"infinite\" (DASH, hlsnative and ISM)\n--retry-sleep [TYPE:]EXPR       Time to sleep between retries in seconds\n                                (optionally) prefixed by the type of retry\n                                (http (default), fragment, file_access,\n                                extractor) to apply the sleep to. Lines starting\n                                with \u0026quot;#\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;;\u0026quot; or \u0026quot;]\u0026quot; are considered as\n                                comments and ignored\n--no-batch-file                 Do not read URLs from batch file (default)\n-P, --paths [TYPES:]PATH        The paths where the files should be\n                                downloaded. Specify the type of file and the\n                                path separated by a colon \u0026quot;:\u0026quot;. All the same\n                                TYPES as --output are supported.\n                                Additionally, you can also provide \u0026quot;home\u0026quot;\n                                (default) and \u0026quot;temp\u0026quot; paths. This\n                                option includes --no-continue\n--no-force-overwrites           Do not overwrite the video, but overwrite\n                                related files (default)\n-c, --continue                  Resume partially downloaded files/fragments\n                                (default)\n--no-continue                   Do not resume partially downloaded\n                                fragments. If the file is not fragmented,\n                                restart download of the entire file\n--part                          Use .part files instead of writing directly\n                                into output file (default)\n--no-part                       Do not use .part files - write directly into\n                                output file\n--mtime                         Use the Last-modified header to set the file\n                                modification time\n--no-mtime                      Do not use the Last-modified header to set\n                                the file modification time (default)\n--write-description             Write video description to a .description file\n--no-write-description          Do not write video description (default)\n--write-info-json               Write video metadata to a .info.json file\n                                (this may contain personal information)\n--no-write-info-json            Do not write video metadata (default)\n--write-playlist-metafiles      Write playlist metadata in addition to the\n                                video metadata when using --write-info-json,\n                                --write-description etc. (default)\n--no-write-playlist-metafiles   Do not write playlist metadata when using\n                                --write-info-json, --write-description etc.\n--clean-info-json               Remove some internal metadata such as\n                                filenames from the infojson (default)\n--no-clean-info-json            Write all fields to the infojson\n--write-comments                Retrieve video comments to be placed in the\n                                infojson. The comments are fetched even\n                                without this option if the extraction is\n                                known to be quick (Alias: --get-comments)\n--no-write-comments             Do not retrieve video comments unless the\n                                extraction is known to be quick (Alias:\n                                --no-get-comments)\n--load-info-json FILE           JSON file containing the video information\n                                (created with the \u0026quot;--write-info-json\u0026quot; option)\n--cookies FILE                  Netscape formatted file to read cookies from\n                                and dump cookie jar in\n--no-cookies                    Do not read/dump cookies from/to file\n                                (default)\n--cookies-from-browser BROWSER[+KEYRING][:PROFILE][::CONTAINER]\n                                The name of the browser to load cookies\n                                from. Currently supported browsers are:\n                                brave, chrome, chromium, edge, firefox,\n                                opera, safari, vivaldi, whale. Optionally,\n                                the KEYRING used for decrypting Chromium\n                                cookies on Linux, the name/path of the\n                                PROFILE to load cookies from, and the\n                                CONTAINER name (if Firefox) (\u0026quot;none\u0026quot; for no\n                                container) can be given with their\n                                respective separators. By default, all\n                                containers of the most recently accessed\n                                profile are used. Currently supported\n                                keyrings are: basictext, gnomekeyring,\n                                kwallet, kwallet5, kwallet6\n--no-cookies-from-browser       Do not load cookies from browser (default)\n--cache-dir DIR                 Location in the filesystem where yt-dlp can\n                                store some downloaded information (such as\n                                client ids and signatures) permanently. By\n                                default ${XDG_CACHE_HOME}/yt-dlp\n--no-cache-dir                  Disable filesystem caching\n--rm-cache-dir                  Delete all filesystem cache files\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e-a, --batch-file FILE           File containing URLs to download (\"-\" for\n                                stdin), one URL per line. data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"--write-link                    Write an internet shortcut file, depending\n                                on the current platform (.url, .webloc or\n                                .desktop). If this option is left\n                                out, yt-dlp will ask interactively\n-2, --twofactor TWOFACTOR       Two-factor authentication code\n-n, --netrc                     Use .netrc authentication data\n--netrc-location PATH           Location of .netrc authentication data;\n                                either the path or its containing directory.\n                                Defaults to ~/.netrc\n--netrc-cmd NETRC_CMD           Command to execute to get the credentials\n                                for an extractor.\n--video-password PASSWORD       Video-specific password\n--ap-mso MSO                    Adobe Pass multiple-system operator (TV\n                                provider) identifier, use --ap-list-mso for\n                                a list of available MSOs\n--ap-username USERNAME          Multiple-system operator account login\n--ap-password PASSWORD          Multiple-system operator account password.\n                                If this option is left out, yt-dlp will ask\n                                interactively\n--ap-list-mso                   List all supported multiple-system operators\n--client-certificate CERTFILE   Path to client certificate file in PEM\n                                format. May include the private key\n--client-certificate-key KEYFILE\n                                Path to private key file for client\n                                certificate\n--client-certificate-password PASSWORD\n                                Password for client certificate private key,\n                                if encrypted. (currently supported: best (default),\n                                aac, alac, flac, m4a, mp3, opus, vorbis,\n                                wav). You can specify multiple rules using\n                                similar syntax as --remux-video\n--audio-quality QUALITY         Specify ffmpeg audio quality to use when\n                                converting the audio with -x. Insert a value\n                                between 0 (best) and 10 (worst) for VBR or a\n                                specific bitrate like 128K (default 5)\n--remux-video FORMAT            Remux the video into another container if\n                                necessary (currently supported: avi, flv,\n                                gif, mkv, mov, mp4, webm, aac, aiff, alac,\n                                flac, m4a, mka, mp3, ogg, opus, vorbis,\n                                wav). If the target container does not\n                                support the video/audio codec, remuxing will\n                                fail. You can specify multiple rules; e.g.\n                                \u0026quot;aac\u0026gt;m4a/mov\u0026gt;mp4/mkv\u0026quot; will remux aac to m4a,\n                                mov to mp4 and anything else to mkv\n--recode-video FORMAT           Re-encode the video into another format if\n                                necessary. The syntax and supported formats\n                                are the same as --remux-video\n--postprocessor-args NAME:ARGS  Give these arguments to the postprocessors.\n                                Specify the postprocessor/executable name\n                                and the arguments separated by a colon \u0026quot;:\u0026quot;\n                                to give the argument to the specified\n                                postprocessor/executable. Supported PP are:\n                                Merger, ModifyChapters, SplitChapters,\n                                ExtractAudio, VideoRemuxer, VideoConvertor,\n                                Metadata, EmbedSubtitle, EmbedThumbnail,\n                                SubtitlesConvertor, ThumbnailsConvertor,\n                                FixupStretched, FixupM4a, FixupM3u8,\n                                FixupTimestamp and FixupDuration. The\n                                supported executables are: AtomicParsley,\n                                FFmpeg and FFprobe. You can also specify\n                                \u0026quot;PP+EXE:ARGS\u0026quot; to give the arguments to the\n                                specified executable only when being used by\n                                the specified postprocessor. Additionally,\n                                for ffmpeg/ffprobe, \u0026quot;_i\u0026quot;/\u0026quot;_o\u0026quot; can be\n                                appended to the prefix optionally followed\n                                by a number to pass the argument before the\n                                specified input/output file, e.g. --ppa\n                                \u0026quot;Merger+ffmpeg_i1:-v quiet\u0026quot;. You can use\n                                this option multiple times to give different\n                                arguments to different postprocessors.\n                                (Alias: --ppa)\n-k, --keep-video                Keep the intermediate video file on disk\n                                after post-processing\n--no-keep-video                 Delete the intermediate video file after\n                                post-processing (default)\n--post-overwrites               Overwrite post-processed files (default)\n--no-post-overwrites            Do not overwrite post-processed files\n--embed-subs                    Embed subtitles in the video (only for mp4,\n                                webm and mkv videos)\n--no-embed-subs                 Do not embed subtitles (default)\n--embed-thumbnail               Embed thumbnail in the video as cover art\n--no-embed-thumbnail            Do not embed thumbnail (default)\n--embed-metadata                Embed metadata to the video file. Also\n                                embeds chapters/infojson if present unless\n                                --no-embed-chapters/--no-embed-info-json are\n                                used (Alias: --add-metadata)\n--no-embed-metadata             Do not add metadata to file (default)\n                                (Alias: --no-add-metadata)\n--embed-chapters                Add chapter markers to the video file\n                                (Alias: --add-chapters)\n--no-embed-chapters             Do not add chapter markers (default) (Alias:\n                                --no-add-chapters)\n--embed-info-json               Embed the infojson as an attachment to\n                                mkv/mka video files\n--no-embed-info-json            Do not embed the infojson as an attachment\n                                to the video file\n--parse-metadata [WHEN:]FROM:TO\n                                Parse additional metadata like title/artist\n                                from other fields; see \u0026quot;MODIFYING METADATA\u0026quot;\n                                for details. Supported values of \u0026quot;WHEN\u0026quot; are\n                                the same as that of --use-postprocessor\n                                (default: pre_process)\n--replace-in-metadata [WHEN:]FIELDS REGEX REPLACE\n                                Replace text in a metadata field using the\n                                given regex. This option can be used\n                                multiple times. Supported values of \u0026quot;WHEN\u0026quot;\n                                are the same as that of --use-postprocessor\n                                (default: pre_process)\n--xattrs                        Write metadata to the video file's xattrs\n                                (using Dublin Core and XDG standards)\n--concat-playlist POLICY        Concatenate videos in a playlist. One of\n                                \u0026quot;never\u0026quot;, \u0026quot;always\u0026quot;, or \u0026quot;multi_video\u0026quot;\n                                (default; only when the videos form a single\n                                show). All the video files must have the\n                                same codecs and number of streams to be\n                                concatenable. The \u0026quot;pl_video:\u0026quot; prefix can be\n                                used with \u0026quot;--paths\u0026quot; and \u0026quot;--output\u0026quot; to set\n                                the output filename for the concatenated\n                                files. See \u0026quot;OUTPUT TEMPLATE\u0026quot; for details\n--fixup POLICY                  Automatically correct known faults of the\n                                file. One of never (do nothing), warn (only\n                                emit a warning), detect_or_warn (the\n                                default; fix the file if we can, warn\n                                otherwise), force (try fixing even if the\n                                file already exists)\n--ffmpeg-location PATH          Location of the ffmpeg binary; either the\n                                path to the binary or its containing directory\n--exec [WHEN:]CMD               Execute a command, optionally prefixed with\n                                when to execute it, separated by a \u0026quot;:\u0026quot;.\n                                Supported values of \u0026quot;WHEN\u0026quot; are the same as\n                                that of --use-postprocessor (default:\n                                after_move). The same syntax as the output\n                                template can be used to pass any field as\n                                arguments to the command. If no fields are\n                                passed, %(filepath,_filename|)q is appended\n                                to the end of the command. This option can\n                                be used multiple times\n--no-exec                       Remove any previously defined --exec\n--convert-subs FORMAT           Convert the subtitles to another format\n                                (currently supported: ass, lrc, srt, vtt).\n                                Use \u0026quot;--convert-subs none\u0026quot; to disable\n                                conversion (default) (Alias: --convert-\n                                subtitles)\n--convert-thumbnails FORMAT     Convert the thumbnails to another format\n                                (currently supported: jpg, png, webp). You\n                                can specify multiple rules using similar\n                                syntax as \u0026quot;--remux-video\u0026quot;. Use \u0026quot;--convert-\n                                thumbnails none\u0026quot; to disable conversion\n                                (default)\n--split-chapters                Split video into multiple files based on\n                                internal chapters. The \u0026quot;chapter:\u0026quot; prefix can\n                                be used with \u0026quot;--paths\u0026quot; and \u0026quot;--output\u0026quot; to set\n                                the output filename for the split files. See\n                                \u0026quot;OUTPUT TEMPLATE\u0026quot; for details\n--no-split-chapters             Do not split video based on chapters (default)\n--remove-chapters REGEX         Remove chapters whose title matches the\n                                given regular expression. The syntax is the\n                                same as --download-sections. This option can\n                                be used multiple times\n--no-remove-chapters            Do not remove any chapters from the file\n                                (default)\n--force-keyframes-at-cuts       Force keyframes at cuts when\n                                downloading/splitting/removing sections.\n                                This is slow due to needing a re-encode, but\n                                the resulting video may have fewer artifacts\n                                around the cuts\n--no-force-keyframes-at-cuts    Do not force keyframes around the chapters\n                                when cutting/splitting (default)\n--use-postprocessor NAME[:ARGS]\n                                The (case-sensitive) name of plugin\n                                postprocessors to be enabled, and\n                                (optionally) arguments to be passed to it,\n                                separated by a colon \u0026quot;:\u0026quot;. ARGS are a\n                                semicolon \u0026quot;;\u0026quot; delimited list of NAME=VALUE.\n                                The \u0026quot;when\u0026quot; argument determines when the\n                                postprocessor is invoked. It can be one of\n                                \u0026quot;pre_process\u0026quot; (after video extraction),\n                                \u0026quot;after_filter\u0026quot; (after video passes filter),\n                                \u0026quot;video\u0026quot; (after --format; before\n                                --print/--output), \u0026quot;before_dl\u0026quot; (before each\n                                video download), \u0026quot;post_process\u0026quot; (after each\n                                video download; default), \u0026quot;after_move\u0026quot;\n                                (after moving the video file to its final\n                                location), \u0026quot;after_video\u0026quot; (after downloading\n                                and processing all formats of a video), or\n                                \u0026quot;playlist\u0026quot; (at end of playlist). This option\n                                can be used multiple times to add different\n                                postprocessors\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e-x, --extract-audio             Convert video files to audio-only files\n                                (requires ffmpeg and ffprobe)\n--audio-format FORMAT           Format to convert the audio to when -x is\n                                used. Available\n                                categories are sponsor, intro, outro,\n                                selfpromo, preview, filler, interaction,\n                                music_offtopic, hook, poi_highlight,\n                                chapter, all and default (=all). You can\n                                prefix the category with a \u0026quot;-\u0026quot; to exclude\n                                it. See [1] for descriptions of the\n                                categories. E.g. --sponsorblock-mark\n                                all,-preview\n                                [1] https://wiki.sponsor.ajay.app/w/Segment_Categories\n--sponsorblock-remove CATS      SponsorBlock categories to be removed from\n                                the video file, separated by commas. If a\n                                category is present in both mark and remove,\n                                remove takes precedence. The syntax and\n                                available categories are the same as for\n                                --sponsorblock-mark except that \u0026quot;default\u0026quot;\n                                refers to \u0026quot;all,-filler\u0026quot; and poi_highlight,\n                                chapter are not available\n--sponsorblock-chapter-title TEMPLATE\n                                An output template for the title of the\n                                SponsorBlock chapters created by\n                                --sponsorblock-mark. The only available\n                                fields are start_time, end_time, category,\n                                categories, name, category_names. Defaults\n                                to \u0026quot;[SponsorBlock]: %(category_names)l\u0026quot;\n--no-sponsorblock               Disable both --sponsorblock-mark and\n                                --sponsorblock-remove\n--sponsorblock-api URL          SponsorBlock API location, defaults to\n                                https://sponsor.ajay.app\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--sponsorblock-mark CATS        SponsorBlock categories to create chapters\n                                for, separated by commas. Available\n                                categories are sponsor, intro, outro,\n                                selfpromo, preview, filler, interaction,\n                                music_offtopic, hook, poi_highlight,\n                                chapter, all and default (=all). You can\n                                prefix the category with a \"-\" to exclude\n                                it. See [1] for descriptions of the\n                                categories. E.g. --sponsorblock-mark\n                                all,-preview\n                                [1] https://wiki.sponsor.ajay.app/w/Segment_Categories\n--sponsorblock-remove CATS      SponsorBlock categories to be removed from\n                                the video file, separated by commas. If a\n                                category is present in both mark and remove,\n                                remove takes precedence. The syntax and\n                                available categories are the same as for\n                                --sponsorblock-mark except that \"default\"\n                                refers to \"all,-filler\" and poi_highlight,\n                                chapter are not available\n--sponsorblock-chapter-title TEMPLATE\n                                An output template for the title of the\n                                SponsorBlock chapters created by\n                                --sponsorblock-mark. The only available\n                                fields are start_time, end_time, category,\n                                categories, name, category_names. Defaults\n                                to \"[SponsorBlock]: %(category_names)l\"\n--no-sponsorblock               Disable both --sponsorblock-mark and\n                                --sponsorblock-remove\n--sponsorblock-api URL          SponsorBlock API location, defaults to\n                                https://sponsor.ajay.app\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote\u003c/strong\u003e: Options in a configuration file are just the same options aka switches used in regular command line calls; thus there \u003cstrong\u003emust be no whitespace\u003c/strong\u003e after \u003ccode\u003e-\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e--\u003c/code\u003e, e.g. \u003ccode\u003e-o\u003c/code\u003e or They must also be quoted when necessary, as if it were a UNIX shell.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYou can use \u003ccode\u003e--ignore-config\u003c/code\u003e if you want to disable all configuration files for a particular yt-dlp run. If \u003ccode\u003e--ignore-config\u003c/code\u003e is found inside any configuration file, no further configuration will be loaded. For example, having the option in the portable configuration file prevents loading of home, user, and system configurations. Additionally, (for backward compatibility) if \u003ccode\u003e--ignore-config\u003c/code\u003e is found inside the system configuration file, the user configuration is not loaded.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch3 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConfiguration file encoding\u003c/h3\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-configuration-file-encoding\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Configuration file encoding\" href=\"#configuration-file-encoding\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe configuration files are decoded according to the UTF BOM if present, and in the encoding from system locale otherwise.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIf you want your file to be decoded differently, add \u003ccode\u003e# coding: ENCODING\u003c/code\u003e to the beginning of the file (e.g. \u003ccode\u003e# coding: shift-jis\u003c/code\u003e). You can achieve this using a \u003ca href=\"https://stackoverflow.com/tags/.netrc/info\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e.netrc\u003c/code\u003e file\u003c/a\u003e on a per-extractor basis. For that, you will need to create a \u003ccode\u003e.netrc\u003c/code\u003e file in \u003ccode\u003e--netrc-location\u003c/code\u003e and restrict permissions to read/write by only you:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"touch ${HOME}/.netrc\nchmod a-rwx,u+rw ${HOME}/.netrc\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003etouch ${HOME}/.netrc\nchmod a-rwx,u+rw ${HOME}/.netrc\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAfter that, you can add credentials for an extractor in the following format, where \u003cem\u003eextractor\u003c/em\u003e is the name of the extractor in lowercase:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"machine \u0026lt;extractor\u0026gt; This is done by providing the \u003ccode\u003e--netrc-cmd\u003c/code\u003e parameter, it shall output the credentials in the netrc format and return \u003ccode\u003e0\u003c/code\u003e on success, other values will be treated as an error. \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e in the command will be replaced by the name of the extractor to make it possible to select the credentials for the right extractor.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eE.g. \u003ccode\u003e${VARIABLE}\u003c/code\u003e/\u003ccode\u003e$VARIABLE\u003c/code\u003e on UNIX and \u003ccode\u003e%VARIABLE%\u003c/code\u003e on Windows; but is always shown as \u003ccode\u003e${VARIABLE}\u003c/code\u003e in this documentation\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eyt-dlp also allows using UNIX-style variables on Windows for path-like options; e.g. \u003ccode\u003e--output\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e--config-locations\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf unset, \u003ccode\u003e${XDG_CONFIG_HOME}\u003c/code\u003e defaults to \u003ccode\u003e~/.config\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e${XDG_CACHE_HOME}\u003c/code\u003e to \u003ccode\u003e~/.cache\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOn Windows, \u003ccode\u003e~\u003c/code\u003e points to \u003ccode\u003e${HOME}\u003c/code\u003e if present; or, \u003ccode\u003e${USERPROFILE}\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e${HOMEDRIVE}${HOMEPATH}\u003c/code\u003e otherwise\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eOn Windows, \u003ccode\u003e${USERPROFILE}\u003c/code\u003e generally points to \u003ccode\u003eC:\\Users\\\u0026lt;user name\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e${APPDATA}\u003c/code\u003e to \u003ccode\u003e${USERPROFILE}\\AppData\\Roaming\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch1 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eOUTPUT TEMPLATE\u003c/h1\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-output-template\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: OUTPUT TEMPLATE\" href=\"#output-template\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe \u003ccode\u003e-o\u003c/code\u003e option is used to indicate a template for the output file names while \u003ccode\u003e-P\u003c/code\u003e option is used to specify the path each type of file should be saved to.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003etl;dr:\u003c/strong\u003e \u003ca href=\"#output-template-examples\"\u003enavigate me to examples\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe simplest usage of \u003ccode\u003e-o\u003c/code\u003e is not to set any template arguments when downloading a single file, like in \u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp -o funny_video.flv \"https://some/video\"\u003c/code\u003e (hard-coding file extension like this is \u003cem\u003enot\u003c/em\u003e recommended and could break some post-processing).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eIt may however also contain special sequences that will be replaced when downloading each video. The special sequences may be formatted according to \u003ca href=\"https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#printf-style-string-formatting\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003ePython string formatting operations\u003c/a\u003e, e.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(NAME)s\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e%(NAME)05d\u003c/code\u003e. To clarify, that is a percent symbol followed by a name in parentheses, followed by formatting operations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe field names themselves (the part inside the parenthesis) can also have some special formatting:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003col dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eObject traversal\u003c/strong\u003e: The dictionaries and lists available in metadata can be traversed by using a dot \u003ccode\u003e.\u003c/code\u003e separator; e.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(tags.0)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(subtitles.en.-1.ext)s\u003c/code\u003e. You can do Python slicing with colon \u003ccode\u003e:\u003c/code\u003e; E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(id.3:7)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(id.6:2:-1)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(formats.:.format_id)s\u003c/code\u003e. Curly braces \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e can be used to build dictionaries with only specific keys; e.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(formats.:.{format_id,height})#j\u003c/code\u003e. An empty field name \u003ccode\u003e%()s\u003c/code\u003e refers to the entire infodict; e.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(.{id,title})s\u003c/code\u003e. Note that all the fields that become available using this method are not listed below. Use \u003ccode\u003e-j\u003c/code\u003e to see such fields\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eArithmetic\u003c/strong\u003e: Simple arithmetic can be done on numeric fields using \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e-\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e*\u003c/code\u003e. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(playlist_index+10)03d\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(n_entries+1-playlist_index)d\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDate/time Formatting\u003c/strong\u003e: Date/time fields can be formatted according to \u003ca href=\"https://docs.python.org/3/library/datetime.html#strftime-and-strptime-format-codes\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003estrftime formatting\u003c/a\u003e by specifying it separated from the field name using a \u003ccode\u003e\u0026gt;\u003c/code\u003e. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(duration\u0026gt;%H-%M-%S)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(upload_date\u0026gt;%Y-%m-%d)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(epoch-3600\u0026gt;%H-%M-%S)s\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eAlternatives\u003c/strong\u003e: Alternate fields can be specified separated with a \u003ccode\u003e,\u003c/code\u003e. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(release_date\u0026gt;%Y,upload_date\u0026gt;%Y|Unknown)s\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eReplacement\u003c/strong\u003e: A replacement value can be specified using a \u003ccode\u003e\u0026amp;\u003c/code\u003e separator according to the \u003ca href=\"https://docs.python.org/3/library/string.html#format-specification-mini-language\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003estr.format\u003c/code\u003e mini-language\u003c/a\u003e. If the field is \u003cem\u003enot\u003c/em\u003e empty, this replacement value will be used instead of the actual field content. This is done after alternate fields are considered; thus the replacement is used if \u003cem\u003eany\u003c/em\u003e of the alternative fields is \u003cem\u003enot\u003c/em\u003e empty. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(chapters\u0026amp;has chapters|no chapters)s\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003e%(title\u0026amp;TITLE={:\u0026gt;20}|NO TITLE)s\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eDefault\u003c/strong\u003e: A literal default value can be specified for when the field is empty using a \u003ccode\u003e|\u003c/code\u003e separator. This overrides \u003ccode\u003e--output-na-placeholder\u003c/code\u003e. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(uploader|Unknown)s\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eMore Conversions\u003c/strong\u003e: In addition to the normal format types \u003ccode\u003ediouxXeEfFgGcrs\u003c/code\u003e, yt-dlp additionally supports converting to \u003ccode\u003eB\u003c/code\u003e = \u003cstrong\u003eB\u003c/strong\u003eytes, \u003ccode\u003ej\u003c/code\u003e = \u003cstrong\u003ej\u003c/strong\u003eson (flag \u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e for pretty-printing, \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e for Unicode), \u003ccode\u003eh\u003c/code\u003e = HTML escaping, \u003ccode\u003el\u003c/code\u003e = a comma-separated \u003cstrong\u003el\u003c/strong\u003eist (flag \u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e for \u003ccode\u003e\\n\u003c/code\u003e newline-separated), \u003ccode\u003eq\u003c/code\u003e = a string \u003cstrong\u003eq\u003c/strong\u003euoted for the terminal (flag \u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e to split a list into different arguments), \u003ccode\u003eD\u003c/code\u003e = add \u003cstrong\u003eD\u003c/strong\u003eecimal suffixes (e.g. 10M) (flag \u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e to use 1024 as factor), and \u003ccode\u003eS\u003c/code\u003e = \u003cstrong\u003eS\u003c/strong\u003eanitize as filename (flag \u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e for restricted)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eUnicode normalization\u003c/strong\u003e: The format type \u003ccode\u003eU\u003c/code\u003e can be used for NFC \u003ca href=\"https://docs.python.org/3/library/unicodedata.html#unicodedata.normalize\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003eUnicode normalization\u003c/a\u003e. The alternate form flag (\u003ccode\u003e#\u003c/code\u003e) changes the normalization to NFD and the conversion flag \u003ccode\u003e+\u003c/code\u003e can be used for NFKC/NFKD compatibility equivalence normalization. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(title)+.100U\u003c/code\u003e is NFKC\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo summarize, the general syntax for a field is:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"%(name[.keys][addition][\u0026gt;strf][,alternate][\u0026amp;replacement][|default])[flags][width][.precision][length]type\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003e%(name[.keys][addition][\u0026gt;strf][,alternate][\u0026amp;replacement][|default])[flags][width][.precision][length]type\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAdditionally, you can set different output templates for the various metadata files separately from the general output template by specifying the type of file followed by the template separated by a colon \u003ccode\u003e:\u003c/code\u003e. The different file types supported are \u003ccode\u003esubtitle\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ethumbnail\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003edescription\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eannotation\u003c/code\u003e (deprecated), \u003ccode\u003einfojson\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003elink\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epl_thumbnail\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epl_description\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epl_infojson\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003echapter\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epl_video\u003c/code\u003e. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e-o \"%(title)s.%(ext)s\" -o \"thumbnail:%(title)s\\%(title)s.%(ext)s\"\u003c/code\u003e will put the thumbnails in a folder with the same name as the video. If any of the templates is empty, that type of file will not be written. E.g. \u003ccode\u003e--write-thumbnail -o \"thumbnail:\"\u003c/code\u003e will write thumbnails only for playlists and not for video.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-outtmpl-postprocess-note\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote\u003c/strong\u003e: Due to post-processing (i.e. merging etc.), the actual output filename might differ. Use \u003ccode\u003e--print after_move:filepath\u003c/code\u003e to get the name after all post-processing is complete.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eThe available fields are:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eid\u003c/code\u003e (string): Video identifier\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etitle\u003c/code\u003e (string): Video title\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003efulltitle\u003c/code\u003e (string): Video title ignoring live timestamp and generic title\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eext\u003c/code\u003e (string): Video filename extension\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ealt_title\u003c/code\u003e (string): A secondary title of the video\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003edescription\u003c/code\u003e (string): The description of the video\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003edisplay_id\u003c/code\u003e (string): An alternative identifier for the video\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003euploader\u003c/code\u003e (string): Full name of the video uploader\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003euploader_id\u003c/code\u003e (string): Nickname or id of the video uploader\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003euploader_url\u003c/code\u003e (string): URL to the video uploader's profile\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003elicense\u003c/code\u003e (string): License name the video is licensed under\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ecreators\u003c/code\u003e (list): The creators of the video\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ecreator\u003c/code\u003e (string): The creators of the video; comma-separated\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003etimestamp\u003c/code\u003e (numeric): UNIX timestamp of the moment the video became available\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eupload_date\u003c/code\u003e (string): Video upload date in UTC (YYYYMMDD)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003erelease_timestamp\u003c/code\u003e (numeric): UNIX timestamp of the moment the video was UTC\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003echannel\u003c/code\u003e (string): Full name of the channel the video is uploaded (string): Length of the video (HH:mm:ss)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eview_count\u003c/code\u003e (numeric): How many users have watched the video on the this field cannot be used)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eage_limit\u003c/code\u003e (numeric): Age restriction for the video (years)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003elive_status\u003c/code\u003e (string): One of \"not_live\", \"is_live\", \"is_upcoming\", \"was_live\", \"post_live\" (was live, but VOD is not yet processed)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eis_live\u003c/code\u003e (boolean): Whether this video is a live stream or a fixed-length \"public\"\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003emedia_type\u003c/code\u003e (string): The type of media as classified by the site, e.g. \"episode\", \"clip\", dir=\"auto\"\u003eEach aforementioned sequence when referenced in an output template will be replaced by the actual value corresponding to the sequence name. E.g. for \u003ccode\u003e-o %(title)s-%(id)s.%(ext)s\u003c/code\u003e and an mp4 video with title \u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp test video\u003c/code\u003e and id \u003ccode\u003eBaW_jenozKc\u003c/code\u003e, this will result in a \u003ccode\u003eyt-dlp test video-BaW_jenozKc.mp4\u003c/code\u003e file created in the current directory.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eNote\u003c/strong\u003e: Some of the sequences are not guaranteed to be present, since they depend on the metadata obtained by a particular extractor. Such sequences will be replaced with placeholder value provided with \u003ccode\u003e--output-na-placeholder\u003c/code\u003e (\u003ccode\u003eNA\u003c/code\u003e by default).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eTip\u003c/strong\u003e: Look at the \u003ccode\u003e-j\u003c/code\u003e output to identify which fields are available for the particular URL\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eFor numeric sequences, you can use \u003ca href=\"https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#printf-style-string-formatting\" rel=\"nofollow\"\u003enumeric related formatting\u003c/a\u003e; e.g. \u003ccode\u003e%(view_count)05d\u003c/code\u003e will result in a string with view count padded with zeros up to 5 characters, like in \u003ccode\u003e00042\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eOutput templates can also contain arbitrary hierarchical path, e.g. \u003ccode\u003e-o \"%(playlist)s/%(playlist_index)s - %(title)s.%(ext)s\"\u003c/code\u003e which will result in downloading each video in a directory corresponding to this path template. Any missing directory will be automatically created for you.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eTo use percent literals in an output template use \u003ccode\u003e%%\u003c/code\u003e.
